---
title: "LVPM: Upgrades Wubi installs to dedicated-partition Ubuntu installs"
date: 2007-05-09
forum: Outdated Tutorials &amp; Tips
---

### Post by tuxcantfly on 2007-05-09
[COLOR="Red"]_***LVPM currently does not work with installs generated by Wubi 10.04 (patches welcome). If you wish to do a standard install of Ubuntu without a CD, please use [UNetbootin](http://unetbootin.sourceforge.net/) [http://unetbootin.sourceforge.net](http://unetbootin.sourceforge.net) instead. ***_[/COLOR]

LVPM's website and screenshot-based guide is at [http://lubi.sourceforge.net/lvpm.html](http://lubi.sourceforge.net/lvpm.html)

LVPM currently supports installations generated by Wubi 8.04, Wubi 7.10, Wubi 7.04, and Lubi 7.04. It has not been updated to work with newer versions (8.10, 9.04, 9.10, 10.04), patches are welcome. Please use the "Alternative Instructions" (see below) instead.

**Rationale for using LVPM to transfer your Wubi install to a real partition**

A major feature of Wubi is that it installs Ubuntu onto a virtual disk, eliminating the hassles and risks of repartitioning. While such an install is adequate for everyday use, there are several advantages to having a "real" Ubuntu installation, that is, one in a dedicated partition, rather than a virtual disk on your Windows install.

1. Full independence from Windows: Wubi relies on Windows to store its virtual disks, and for its bootloader. Thus, should you decide that Ubuntu serves your needs and you no longer need Windows, you cannot simply delete your Windows partition, as that will remove your Wubi install as well. To switch entirely to Ubuntu, you will first need to transfer your Wubi install to its own partition by following this guide, and only then can you delete your Windows partition.

2. Performance boost: There is a slight hard drive performance penalty in a Wubi install due to the usage of virtual disks. While it shouldn't be noticeable in everyday usage, if you regularly edit and copy large files, such as in movie editing, there should be a speed improvement if you transfer your Wubi install to a dedicated partition.

3. Regain hibernation functionality: Even if your hardware supports hibernation under Ubuntu, you will be unable to do so in Wubi, since the swap is within a virtual drive. However, if you transfer your install to a real partition, you will have dedicated swap, so you will be able to hibernate if your hardware supports it normally under Ubuntu (check in the forums for information on any particular hardware models).

**Before starting...**

Always remember to back up data, just in case something happens. Back up to a USB flash drive, CD/DVD, anywhere EXCEPT your hard drive.

Also make sure you have a spare partition to install to. To do this, just use the [Partition Manager tool](http://sourceforge.net/project/showfiles.php?group_id=198821) (short video tutorial at [http://blip.tv/file/331394](http://blip.tv/file/331394) ) to resize the Windows partition with GParted and create a new primary partition formatted as ext3. You'll also need to create another partition with a size greater than your ram size, and format it as swap.

**Creating new partitions and resizing existing ones**

This is only required if you don't already have a spare partition to install to. Also make sure you have a swap partition of greater size than your RAM memory, in addition to the partition you will install Linux to (the filesystem type for the main partition doesn't matter, it'll be made ext3 anyhow, just make sure the swap partition is formatted as swap or it won't be used). If you do, just move on to the next section.

To do this, you can use the [Partition Manager tool](http://sourceforge.net/project/showfiles.php?group_id=198821) (short video tutorial at [http://blip.tv/file/331394](http://blip.tv/file/331394) ), boot it up and open GParted, then follow the guide at [http://gparted.sourceforge.net/larry/resize/resizing.htm](http://gparted.sourceforge.net/larry/resize/resizing.htm)

Resize your Windows partitions (NTFS) and create a new primary partition (format doesn't matter, it'll be formatted ext3 by LVPM, but it should be at least as large as the Wubi virtual disks, at least 5 GB) and a swap partition (of greater size than the amount of RAM memory). Also note what the device string of the new system (not swap) partition is (something like /dev/sdb1, /dev/hda2); you'll need it later.

ONLY resize the Windows (NTFS) partition, DON'T delete it just yet, even if you plan on getting rid of Windows, because your Wubi install is still on it.

**Installing and running LVPM, the Loopmounted Virtual Partition Manager**

You can either follow my step-by-step **video tutorial** at [http://blip.tv/file/331947](http://blip.tv/file/331947), a screenshot-based guide at [http://lubi.sourceforge.net/lvpm.html](http://lubi.sourceforge.net/lvpm.html) or follow the instrctions below:

Boot the Ubuntu install created by Wubi/Lubi, and download and install the latest lvpm deb package.

[http://lubi.sourceforge.net/lvpm-latest.deb](http://lubi.sourceforge.net/lvpm-latest.deb)

Once installed, open Applications -> System Tools -> LVPM, and select either the "transfer" option, and select a partition to install to. **DO NOT SELECT A PARTITION WITH ANY IMPORTANT DATA ON IT; IT WILL BE WIPED OUT. ALSO NOTE THAT GRUB WILL BE INSTALLED TO THE MBR.** If you want to resize your virtual disks, rather than transfer them to dedicated partitions, use the "resize" option.

Now, reboot and hope that it works, if you run into some horrible boot error, plop in the Super Grub Disk, and hopefully, you should be able to boot your system.

**Getting rid of the original Wubi install (optional)**

If you're satisfied with your new real-partition install, and have no need to keep your original Wubi install, just boot Windows, go to "Add/Remove Programs", select Wubi, and press "Uninstall", and you'll be left only with your real-partition Ubuntu installation.

**Getting rid of Windows entirely (optional)**

AFTER you have transferred the Wubi install to a real partition, and it is working, boot the [Partition Manager tool](http://sourceforge.net/project/showfiles.php?group_id=198821), open GParted, delete the Windows (NTFS) partition, and follow the guide at [http://gparted.sourceforge.net/larry/tips/gfs.htm](http://gparted.sourceforge.net/larry/tips/gfs.htm) to expand your ext3 partition to use up the free space left by the deleted Windows (NTFS) partition.

**Resizing virtual disks using LVPM**

Run LVPM, and once the menu appears, select "resize" (to resize the root virtual disk, which contains both /home and the system files).

Input the new size, in MB, of the virtual disk.

Wait until the program finishes creating a new disks file and copying files from original home disk file; it will pop up a final instruction window instructing to backup the original home disk file and renaming the newly created disk file

Boot into windows and navigate to c:\wubi\disks, move the old virtual disk to a different folder as backup, and rename new.virtual.disk to root.virtual.disk

Reboot into ubuntu

If everything works, make sure you leave your vote on the poll, and if there's some error in the instructions or something didn't work, make sure leave a comment.

_[COLOR="Red"]**Alternative Instructions**[/COLOR] _

It's possible to migrate Wubi installs (any version, works on both 7.04 or 7.10), data, and settings (apps can be quickly reinstalled via apt-get) to dedicated-partition installs using an alternative approach (use this if LVPM fails), which also doesn't require a CD:

1. Create 3 new partitions with the [Partition Manager](http://lubi.sourceforge.net/lvpm.html) ([download](http://sourceforge.net/project/showfiles.php?group_id=198821&package_id=240127)): a 5-10 GB (ext3 format) partition to use as root (/), a ~1 GB (equal to RAM size) (swap format) partition to use as swap, and make the rest a (ext3 format) partition to use as /home.

2. Boot back into the Wubi-generated Ubuntu install, mount the new partition that will be used as /home in the dedicated-partition install to /media/disk, and copy the contents of the current /home recursively over to the new partition:

```
rsync -avx /home/ /media/disk
```

Additionally, if you want to avoid the hassle of manually reinstalling all the packages you currently have installed, run:

```
dpkg --get-selections > selections.dpkg
```

That'll generate a list of packages you have installed (back up that list to somewhere safe); after reinstalling the system, just open Synaptic, go file > read markings, select that file that was generated (selections.dpkg), press apply, and it'll reinstall all the software you have on your current system (details [here](http://www.karkomaonline.com/index.php/2006/02/24/package-management-in-debian/)).

3. Reboot into Windows, and install [UNetbootin](http://unetbootin.sourceforge.net) ([download](http://unetbootin.sourceforge.net/unetbootin-windows-latest.php)).

Download and install the .exe version, reboot, then select "UNetbootin" at the boot menu, then the Ubuntu installer will start up. After that, just follow the standard Ubuntu installation process ([guide](http://www.howtoforge.com/unetbootin_windows_ubuntu_fedora)), just make sure that at the "partitioning" stage, select the "manual" option, and make sure tospecify the appropriate mountpoints (make sure the partition you copies /home to is mounted at /home, and make sure it doesn't get formatted). After that, wait for Ubuntu to be downloaded and installed from the net (it'll take a long time if you're on a slow connection, just give it a few hours to complete).

4. Once done installing, reboot back, and your new dedicated-partition Ubuntu install, complete with data and settings preserved, should be there. You can re-install the individual applications via apt-get. Once done, you can reboot back into Windows and remove the UNetbootin installer (it'll prompt on startup), and remove Wubi, then you'll be done.

**NOTES**

If you ever get a GRUB error, or can't boot one of your operating systems, boot up the Super Grub Disk [http://supergrub.forjamari.linex.org/](http://supergrub.forjamari.linex.org/) and it will allow you to repair GRUB and be able to boot Windows and Ubuntu.

---

### Post by tuxcantfly on 2007-05-10
I have now created a couple of scripts that automate this process, note that they haven't yet been extensively tested, proceed with care...

Before running these scripts, make sure that you have already done the resizing of the partitions, see post above for details.

Also, it should be run while in a livecd environment, not whjile booted into the Wubi-generated Ubuntu install.

Download the files at [http://cutlersoftware.com/ubuntusetup/lupin2partition](http://cutlersoftware.com/ubuntusetup/lupin2partition) and [http://cutlersoftware.com/ubuntusetup/lupin2partitiongui](http://cutlersoftware.com/ubuntusetup/lupin2partitiongui)

Then make them executable:

```
chmod +x ./lupin2partition*
```

Then place them into /usr/bin:

```
sudo mv ./lupin2partition /usr/bin
```

Then start the wizard:

```
sudo lupin2partitiongui
```

Or if you prefer to use the command line:

```
sudo lupin2partition
```

Report any errors, bugs, issues, etc. with the scripts here...

### Post by tuxcantfly on 2007-06-22
> Is it possible to use this to get hibernate/suspend working? (currently doesn't work under Wubi)

It'll depend on your hardware; even normal ubuntu installs don't support suspend or hibernate on a lot of hardware, but since the swap is on a dedicated partition, it should be no different from a standard install; if the hardware supports suspend/hiberate on a normal ubuntu install, it'll support it here.

> Also..what if I want to keep the Vista boot loader and not use Grub?

Vista bootloader can only boot Windows, Grub is needed to boot Ubuntu and other operating systems. Using the chainloader approach described above, you can boot both Ubuntu and Windows with grub, so I don't see what the problem with using grub would be... Of course, you could use the Vista bootloader to boot GRLDR, the same approach that the standard Wubi does, and remove Grub from the MBR, and that'll work too, but that's basically pointless, since it's more error-prone, increases boot times, and has no practical advantages over just using GRUB to chainload the Vista bootloader...

---

### Post by tuxcantfly on 2007-06-24
> Yeah I understand that, though I thought there was currently a hibernate issue with Wubi

Yes, that's what I meant. There's a hibernation issue with Wubi due to the usage of loopmounted disks, but once you transfer the install to a real partition using LVPM (and remember to create a swap partition that is greater than or equal to your ram size prior to installing), hibernation should work (if your hardware would support it under a standard Ubuntu install, that is)
> 
And ok, I was just worried since I've read that Vista is extremely picky about things like its partition and what not.

So long as you have a free partition (or make one by resizing existing ones), and you don't tell LVPM to install to the Vista partition, you shouldn't have any issues with that; Vista shouldn't be impacted by this; GRUB will simply chainload the Vista bootloader and it will boot as usual

> sudo gedit doesn't work and I can't seem to get anything working through localhost.

Very strange error, I don't think it could be related to Wubi or Lubi, since those are only supposed to impact the disk layout and partitioning-related issues, but if you don't get that issue on a standard Ubuntu install, make sure to report it, it could be some bug we didn't notice...

### Post by Spegelius on 2007-06-30
Moved my Feisty installation to real partition yesterday. Had to tinker a bit to get it working:
I booted Wubi from USB drive (by mistake). I had taken a backup of Wubi folder to USB drive and my laptop decided to use it as boot drive. (BTW, i am also having problem with wubildr not being found from laptops hd, works only from the USB drive...)
So i used gparted in Wubi and made changes to laptop HD (/dev/sdb). Shrinked the only NTFS partition and created swap and one big ext3 partition. After that downloaded lvpm and executed it. After two hours of waiting, i got some error about not enough space. The problem was that the script failed to mount /dev/sdb2 to /media/tdm, because gnome had allready mounted to new partition automatically. Still, the script continued and began to fill the virtual drive with contents of itself... ;). 
I tried again, this time /dev/sdb2 unmounted. This time it worked. Only problem was that grub set the boot drive to hd(1,1) which doesn't work as the USB drive isn't usually connected and i had to manually change it to hd(0,1).

Speed: boot is bit faster, hard to notice. Normal use, again bit of improvement. But in heavy disk related use (mixed accesses to both virtual drives and the mounted host NTFS partition) there's definite improvement. It seems that system is also more responsive during heavy use.
Wubi really is worth trying; it made me test Linux after few years of laziness. I could test it without needing to juggle partitions. Now that i am using Ubuntu almost all the time, i'm thinking getting rid of Windows.

---

### Post by Spegelius on 2007-07-01
Just noticed that lupin-target wasn't properly uninstalled, because apt kept failing. Files /etc/initramfs-tools/update-initramfs.conf and /etc/initramfs-tools/initramfs.conf were allready deleted and lupin-target removal failed on those. Fixed it by creating empty files (sudo touch /etc/initramfs-tools/update-initramfs.conf etc..) and lupin-target was properly removed.

---

### Post by tuxcantfly on 2007-07-01
> Just noticed that lupin-target wasn't properly uninstalled, because apt kept failing. Files /etc/initramfs-tools/update-initramfs.conf and /etc/initramfs-tools/initramfs.conf were allready deleted and lupin-target removal failed on those. Fixed it by creating empty files (sudo touch /etc/initramfs-tools/update-initramfs.conf etc..) and lupin-target was properly removed.

Thanks again for the bug report, seems like that was the issue Epilonsama had, turns out that it wasn't an issue with LVPM itself, but an issue in the lupin-target package introduced in revision 55 (so it only affects 7.04.01, not older versions), so I've fixed it in the lupin devel branch (so it shouldn't be present in future wubi and lubi versions), and also added a hack into the latest lvpm deb package so that it'll properly remove the faulty lupin-target.deb in 7.04.01.

### Post by dndrich on 2007-07-08

---

### Post by tuxcantfly on 2007-07-08
> So what I have now is a computer that will boot to Windows, but no way to duel boot into Ubuntu. Occasionally I am lucky, and can boot to the Ubuntu partition with some command in Super Grub Disk, so I know the Ubuntu partition is OK. So how to I get duel booting to work now?

Seems like something went wrong with the os detection, I'll probably need to do a few tweaks to the lvpm code, doesn't seem to be working in all cases... For now, to fix the bootloader, what you'll have to do is use super grub disk to boot ubuntu, then in a terminal, type in:

```
sudo grub-install "(hd0)"
```

Then you'll only be able to boot ubuntu, but to restore your ability to boot windows, open the grub menu.lst at /boot/grub/menu.lst:
```

sudo gedit /boot/grub/menu.lst
```

and add this line at the end:

```
title Windows
rootnoverify (hd0,0)
makeactive
chainloader +1
boot
```

I'm assuming your ntfs partition is the first partition of the first hard drive, if not, adjust the first line accordingly (first number is drive, second number is partition)

Then reboot, you might need to press ESC when the "grub loading..." screen shows up, you should be presented with a menu, and select the last option (windows) to boot windows, select the first option to boot ubuntu.

### Post by tuxcantfly on 2007-07-08

### Post by dndrich on 2007-07-08
OK, that appeared to work.  I had to hit escape, and I was able to scroll down to get Windows.  Now, how do I get it to work like Wubi did, giving me a choice of Windows or Ubuntu before booting?

---

### Post by tuxcantfly on 2007-07-08
> Now, how do I get it to work like Wubi did, giving me a choice of Windows or Ubuntu before booting?

find the line (towards the beginning of the file) that says:
```

hiddenmenu
```

and change that to:

```
#hiddenmenu
```

if you want to change timeout (how long you'll wait until booting), find the line that says "timeout" and change the number next to it (that's the timeout in seconds)

If you want to change the order, just go to the end of the file, and find the blocks of text that start with "title" (starting with "title Ubuntu kernel 2.6.20-15"), and reorganize the order of the blocks of text; you can get rid of the "recovery mode" and "memtest" options since they aren't really needed unless something breaks...

---

### Post by Depressed Man on 2007-07-11
> **tuxcantfly said:**
> Yes, that's what I meant. There's a hibernation issue with Wubi due to the usage of loopmounted disks, but once you transfer the install to a real partition using LVPM (and remember to create a swap partition that is greater than or equal to your ram size prior to installing), hibernation should work (if your hardware would support it under a standard Ubuntu install, that is)


So long as you have a free partition (or make one by resizing existing ones), and you don't tell LVPM to install to the Vista partition, you shouldn't have any issues with that; Vista shouldn't be impacted by this; GRUB will simply chainload the Vista bootloader and it will boot as usual



Very strange error, I don't think it could be related to Wubi or Lubi, since those are only supposed to impact the disk layout and partitioning-related issues, but if you don't get that issue on a standard Ubuntu install, make sure to report it, it could be some bug we didn't notice...

### Post by tuxcantfly on 2007-07-12
> Hibernate still doesn't work on my laptop though suspend does

That's probably an issue of hardware compatibility; not all hardware supports hibernation under Ubuntu (check the forums for compatibility lists), so your hardware probably supports suspend under Ubuntu, but not hibernate. Anyhow I've stickied this thread since users seem to be reporting success with the latest version, and it's now installed by default as of Wubi/Lubi 7.04.02.

### Post by tuxcantfly on 2007-07-24
**Ignore this post, it's outdated, see the lvpm site for more info on partitionmanager usage and the guide**

I've made a new tool to make the partition resizing portion easier. It is essentially a stripped-down version of Ubuntu with QTParted (used because it has fewer dependencies than GParted), set to boot off the RAM (Much thanks to jdong's [https://wiki.ubuntu.com/BootToRAM](https://wiki.ubuntu.com/BootToRAM) howto). You will need at least 256 MB of RAM to use it, since the entire application is booting and running running from the ramdisk.

First, in you Wubi install, download the package from [http://sourceforge.net/project/showfiles.php?group_id=198821&package_id=240127](http://sourceforge.net/project/showfiles.php?group_id=198821&package_id=240127)

Then cd to the directory you downloaded to, and run:

```
chmod +x ./partitionmanager-1.sh
sudo ./partitionmanager-1.sh
```

Then reboot, and there should be an option in the Wubi GRUB boot menu that says "Partition Manager" (in the 2nd menu that shows up, not the initial Windows NTLDR one). Select that option, let it bootup, and you will be presented with a QTParted GUI to shrink/resize your partitions.

---

### Post by Cyberapoc on 2007-07-27
I've been running wubi ubuntu for a while now and I have to say thank you for making it! I've never been able to run ubuntu straight because of a bug in GRUB working with JMicron RAID, causing it to not recognize my hd. 

Now I'm planning on putting the install on a seperate partition and removing windows vista. The only thing is, I think the errors I got with GRUB will return if I do this. Do you know if this is true and do you have any help you can give me regarding this?

---

### Post by tuxcantfly on 2007-07-27
> Now I'm planning on putting the install on a seperate partition and removing windows vista. The only thing is, I think the errors I got with GRUB will return if I do this. Do you know if this is true and do you have any help you can give me regarding this?

Hmm... pretty strange that GRLDR works but the original GRUB doesn't... anyhow, if the issue is with GRUB itself, then it won't work, though if it was an issue with the Ubuntu installer's configuration of GRUB, it may work. Anyhow, here's what I'd try:

1. Install to a dedicated partition using this guide. Then, BEFORE you reboot open up the file /boot/grub/menu.lst inside the target partition (which I'm assuming is /dev/sda2, the second partition of the first drive, adjust the lines accordingly):

```
sudo mkdir /media/sda2
sudo mount /dev/sda2 /media/sda2
gedit /media/sda2/boot/grub/menu.lst
```

Now look towards the end, you'll see something along these lines:
```

title		Ubuntu, kernel 2.6.20-16-generic
root		(hd0,2)
kernel		/boot/vmlinuz-2.6.20-16-generic root=UUID=e664517b-a99f-4c96-a394-d01be4d9a2e6 ro quiet splash
initrd		/boot/initrd.img-2.6.20-16-generic
quiet
savedefault
```

And copy-paste that into the very end of the file /media/host/wubi/boot/grub/menu.lst, and also remember to change the "timeout 1" towards the beginning of the file /media/host/wubi/boot/grub/menu.lst to "timeout 10" and change "hiddenmenu" to "#hiddenmenu"

2. Then reboot, and you'll probably be presented with a GRUB error, so recover your MBR with the Vista install CD, details at [http://auscoder.com/2007-05-18/restore-vista-mbr-bootloader.html](http://auscoder.com/2007-05-18/restore-vista-mbr-bootloader.html)
3. When the Vista MBR is restored, you'll again see the menu allowing you to select between Vista and Ubuntu. Select Ubuntu. Then you'll see another menu. Select the last entry, and you'll be able to boot the real-partition Ubuntu install.

---

### Post by tuxcantfly on 2007-07-27
> Now I'm planning on putting the install on a seperate partition and removing windows vista.

Note that if you're using GRLDR through the Vista bootloader to boot, you won't be able to remove Vista (since you're using its bootloader), only option I can think of is shrink your RAID partitions a bit, and make a small non-raid partition, and use that to install GRUB to and do the booting from there.

---

### Post by tuxcantfly on 2007-07-31
> One thing is; the second bootmenu requires a hit on Esc, and then I have to select the last entry (the wubi kernels appear in the second menu as well). Somehow I like to automate that process, but I'll figure that out another time

Set "timeout" to 0 in C:\wubi\boot\menu.lst and change the number next to "default" from "0" to the number of the last entry.

---

### Post by tuxcantfly on 2007-07-31
Anyhow, new version of LVPM, based off revision 51, it'll be automatically updated for you when you run the lvpm command if you're using one of the newer versions of Wubi (7.04.02 and above), but if you're running an older version, you'll have to download from the sourceforge download page at [http://sourceforge.net/project/showfiles.php?group_id=198821](http://sourceforge.net/project/showfiles.php?group_id=198821)

Changes/New Features:

* The /etc/fstab file now uses UUID identifiers instead of partition numbers (so that it behaves the same way that the fstab in Ubuntu 7.04 does)
* The original MBR is now backed up to /media/host/MBR-backup (or C:\MBR-backup from Windows), and can easily be restored with the command dd if=/media/host/MBR-backup of=/dev/sda bs=512 count=1
* There is now a -nogrub option that allows LVPM to use your existing bootloader instead of installing GRUB

---

### Post by hh93 on 2007-08-21
Hi All,

Just voted that the howto worked with a bit of tinkering. I thought, i just listed here what i did to migrate wubi unbuntu into real partition (FAT32).

1 prepared system to display Ubuntu boot menu by modifying /media/host/wubi/boot/grub/menu.lst (time out=10,add # to hiddenmenu; tuxcantfy wrote about this. [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=438591&page=4](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=438591&page=4)). The command used:
----gksudo gedit /media/host/wubi/boot/grub/menu.lst
----within the file change time out to 10 and add # to hiddenmenu
2 Reboot into Ubuntu and verify that the modification succeeded to bring out Ubuntu Boot Menu with pressing ESC during 10 sec countdown
3 Boot into Ubuntu Kernel Generic
4 Downloaded sh version of partition manager (partitionmanager-20.sh from sourceforge ([http://sourceforge.net/project/showfiles.php?group_id=198821&package_id=240127&release_id=530586](http://sourceforge.net/project/showfiles.php?group_id=198821&package_id=240127&release_id=530586))). Also downloaded Lvpm deb package (lvpm_60_all.deb)
5 Installed partition manager from terminal (ref. to tuxcantfly direction at [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=438591&page=6](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=438591&page=6)), i just pasted it again below
----- chmod +x ./partitionmanager-1.sh
----- sudo ./partitionmanager-1.sh
6 Once installation finished, reboot into Ubuntu
7. on the 10 seconds countdown pressed ESC to access Ubuntu Boot Menu
8 Boot into partition manager 
9 Selected screen Resolution and Depth, waited till GUI loaded.
10 Clicked Gparted icon
11 Resized Windows Partition
12 Created New 868 MB 'logical partition' as linux swap
13 Created New 12 GiB 'logical partition' as Ext3
14 Applied pending changes
15 Let Gparted finish applying chages and rescan the partition
16 took note of the new Ext3 partition designation (for me it was /dev/hda7)
17 Quit Gparted
18 Turned off Partition Manager by clicking the Power button, select reboot
19 Reboot into windows let it scan the disk and reboot one more time into windows (up to the login screen) to finish disk scan
20 Reboot into Ubuntu
21 Install Lvpm by double clicking on the deb package icon.
22 Check if lvpm correctly installed, by looking for it in Applications --> System tool
23 I ran lvpm from terminal rather than from System tool, to preserve windows boot loader (tuxcantly wrote guide on this [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=438591](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=438591)). Command :
---- sudo lvpm -nogrub /dev/sda7
24 let installation run; the process includes formatting the Ext3 partition, copying files from wubi, and installing grub (apparently grub was still installed even though i specify -nogrub in the command)
25 saw the newly prep'ed partition displayed as drive on the desktop
26 verified that it contains all the folders contained within filesystem under /media/host/wubi. 
27 Reboot
28 This time the computer rebooted into grub
29 I chose to reboot into other operating system : windows to check if windows was ok: it was.
30 Reboot into Ubuntu, seem to be working fine with noticable increase in speed: one applet failed to load though, the Invest Applet, the rest were fine.
31 Verified all application work.

My Laptop :
- Intel Centrino 1500
- 60 GB Fujitsu 
- 512 MB Memory
- Dual Boot FAT32 XP Home + Wubi Ubuntu 

Note:
previous attemps failed due to  failure to install partition manager deb package due to error setting ownership during installation. I tried several workarounds such as rectifying the way windows partition was mounted, changing ownership of foders/files, modifying permission, all failed though.

Cheers!
hh93

I did change the root to (hd0,6), where my ubuntu is, and remove wubi from the referenced directory and get partition manager to work.

It seem as if the program was set to install only from wubi. Was this intended? 

The installation script executed while installing the deb checks to see if it's within a wubi install, based on whether or not /media/host/wubi exists, and if it does, it configures it to boot as wubi, and if it doesn't, it configures it to boot as normal.

Anyhow, I'm presuming that the install you're using at the moment is an LVPM-upgraded Wubi install; does the directory /media/host/wubi exist? If it does, that seems to be the problem; that would be a bug with LVPM causing it to be detected as a Wubi install, though it isn't one; I'll be fixing that by changing the mountpoint to /media/host0 rather than /media/host in LVPM-generated installs to prevent confusion with Wubi.

Anyhow, on a temporary basis, try creating the directory /media/host0

sudo mkdir /media/host0

edit the fstab and change /media/host to /media/host0

then reboot and remove /media/host (it should be empty)

sudo rm -r /media/host

then purge the partitionmanager deb (sudo dpkg --purge partitionmanager), and try installing it again, does anything different happen this time?

---

### Post by tuxcantfly on 2007-08-26
new release, LVPM version 77, new bugfixes:

 * different behavior for the (experimental) -nogrub option, details at [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=3257028](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=3257028)
 * host partition is now mounted to /media/host0 not /media/host to avoid the installation being misdetected as a Wubi install

### Post by mad_ady on 2007-08-29
Hello everyone,

I'd like to say that lvpm worked for me (I used xubuntu 7.04). There were two problems: first when I selected the partition, it didn't say on which partition my current install was (I wonder what would have happened if I chose /dev/sda1 instead of /dev/sda2), and when the install was complete, the new ubuntu didn't mount my swap partition at startup (I fixed it by hand).

Other than that, installing on a real partition instead of running from inside ntfs gave a real performance boost: for instance before, at startup I had about 350MB of RAM used, now, in the same conditions I have about 200MB.

Good job everyone!

---

### Post by tuxcantfly on 2007-08-29
> **mad_ady said:**
> (I wonder what would have happened if I chose /dev/sda1 instead of /dev/sda2)

Don't worry about that, I added some checks to prevent that from happening in the newer versions; if you happen to select your host partition, all that will happen is it'll spit out an error prompt and take you back to the partition selection menu. Then again, though, if you had used the older version (the one that is currently included in Wubi 7.04.04) without having upgraded first, and accidentally selected the wrong partition, yes, it would have wiped out all your data, which is why all users are strongly encouraged not to use the old version and upgrade using the LVPM packages at [http://sourceforge.net/project/showfiles.php?group_id=198821](http://sourceforge.net/project/showfiles.php?group_id=198821) before running.

---

### Post by Anpheus on 2007-09-05
Unbootable. If the LVPM script fails partway through for any reason, attempting to restart it will result in another, more thoroughly failed execution (one would hope the operations it performed would be atomic, or at least not affect my MBR and apparently partition tables, because Lenovo System Recovery won't even start.)

Simply put, that's unacceptable. Please change the script so that all GRUB/boot/partition changes with the exception of formatting the target partition occur only after the user has been prompted to do so.

Also, don't rename wubi to wubi-backup, and don't cut and paste, just copy the files over to the new partition. The second attempt failed miserably because the script couldn't find hundreds of files in various directories, and I noticed that when I went to root, the vmlinuz and other files were -ALL- broken. The result was that on running the script a second time, I turned what might have been a windows-only boot machine into a completely unbootable machine because GRUB completely failed, it reported some errors with my partition table but tried anyway, etc.

---

### Post by tuxcantfly on 2007-09-05
> at least not affect my MBR and apparently partition tables

Obviously it would affect the MBR; where else would a bootloader be installed? When I write "real Ubuntu install" that means that, like a real Ubuntu install, GRUB will be installed to the MBR. But anyhow, I've added in a warning before anything happens that explicitly writes, "LVPM will install Ubuntu to /dev/sda3 (so all data on /dev/sda3 will be wiped out) and GRUB will be installed to the MBR. Proceed?",  hope that satisfies your need for warnings.

> Also, don't rename wubi to wubi-backup, and don't cut and paste

It doesn't do that with the default options. If you're using experimental, unsupported options like -nogrub, expect to have issues. Anyhow I've removed the -nogrub option, hope that prevents people from using it. However, if you were installing using the standard method and options, using the GUI, make sure to post back, since that's a real issue.

> I turned what might have been a windows-only boot machine into a completely unbootable machine because GRUB completely failed

Boot a winxp recovery CD, go into recovery mode (R), type in "fixmbr", that'll get rid of GRUB and make your Windows installation bootable.

---

### Post by tuxcantfly on 2007-09-05
> ... But I have to be able to run LVPM without GRUB installing. That's vital. Can you patch the script or tell me how to do so, all that needs to happen is all the GRUB-related material is removed from the script (not disk.) Keep my MBR intact, copy everything verbatim over to the new partition, and let me figure out how to get Ubuntu to boot from the new partition (and continue to allow me to use the old Wubi-based install until a time of my choosing.) Making it so I can't boot into either OS is not a solution for me. Keeping the Vista MBR intact is vital for me, as I believe the Thinkvantage recovery software requires the Vista MBR. No MBR, no system recovery, and that means I don't use Linux.


become root

```
sudo -s
```

mount drive to /media/tdm

```

tdp=/dev/sda3 # (the target partition)
sdp=/dev/sda2 # (the swap partition)
hostosroot=/dev/sda1 # (the host partition)
mount $tdp /media/tdm
```

copy files over

```
rsync --recursive --links --quiet --specials --devices --group --owner --acls --whole-file --one-file-system /* /media/tdm
```

chroot in and remove lupin-taget

```
chroot /media/tdm << EOT
dpkg --force-all --purge lupin-target
cp /update-initramfs.conf /etc/initramfs-tools/update-initramfs.conf
cp /initramfs.conf /etc/initramfs-tools/initramfs.conf
cp /modules /etc/initramfs-tools/modules
dpkg --force-all --purge lupin-target
mv /update-initramfs.conf /etc/initramfs-tools/update-initramfs.conf
mv /initramfs.conf /etc/initramfs-tools/initramfs.conf
mv /modules /etc/initramfs-tools/modules
dpkg-reconfigure initramfs-tools
update-initramfs -c -k $(uname -r)
update-grub -y
exit
EOT
```

adjust fstab

```

rm /media/tdm/etc/fstab
touch /media/tdm/etc/fstab
rm -r /media/tdm/media/host
mkdir /media/tdm/media/host0
mhostosfstype=$(echo $hostosfstype | sed "s/ntfs/ntfs-3g/")
tdpuuid=$(vol_id -u $tdp)
hostosrootuuid=$(vol_id -u $hostosroot)
echo \
"# <file system> <mount point>   <type>  <options>       <dump>  <pass>
proc            /proc           proc        defaults    0   0
# $tdp
UUID=$tdpuuid     /               $tpf        defaults,errors=remount-ro    0   1
# $hostosroot
UUID=$hostosrootuuid       /media/host0       $mhostosfstype         defaults      0   0
" > /media/tdm/etc/fstab
if [ "$sdp" != "" ];
then
sdpuuid=$(vol_id -u $sdp)
echo \
"
# $sdp
UUID=$sdpuuid      none            swap        sw          0   0
" >> /media/tdm/etc/fstab
fi
```

adjust bootloader afterwards (depends on bootloader you're using)

---

### Post by Anpheus on 2007-09-06
In one of the branching statements you used ```
$tdp = "string"
``` instead of ```
"$tdp" = "string"
```.

The rsync line takes an extremely long time and gives no indication of progress except reporting any errors that occur, I think all the errors it gave were pedantic, failed verification update discarded errors from /sys/power/, /sys/module/, and other system areas.

The lines beginning with ```
chroot /media/tdm << EOT
``` and ending with EOT fail. Errors:
The line "cp /update-initramfs.conf /etc/initramfs-tools/update-initramfs.conf" fails with "cp: cannot stat update-initramfs.conf": no such file or directory. The same error occurs when the script copies initramfs.conf, modules, and when it moves the three files following the second dpkg line.



I'm not going to reboot my laptop until those problems are diagnosed (despite now having a working procedure to restore the Lenovo MBR, I don't want to tempt fate by ending up with an Ubuntu .disk that won't boot, making all of this moot.)



Edit: After a lot of very careful tinkering, I've succeeded in getting the kernel to boot from /dev/sda3 but X fails to start among other things.

Edit: The problem so far is that / is mounted as read only every time I boot into /dev/sda3.

And it's now bootable, I fixed it by editing /etc/fstab to mount / as ext3 (I didn't know if it mattered) and removed errors=remount-ro, and I removed the /wubi/* information from mtab.

### Post by tuxcantfly on 2007-09-07
> **theartak said:**
> So, been using Wubi with kubuntu for a few months now. Love it.  I need to get a new hard drive before I go through the whole full conversion to a partition, 40 GB is a bit of a squeeze for me to have both XP and Kubuntu on board right now.

So I'm trying to use LVPM to expand my home.virtual.disk and I'm a little concerned...I set it for 4000 MB (which, by my math should be 4GB) and set it on its merry little way.  

First problem was that the progress bar only moved to a certain point and stayed there. Not a big deal...figured it was a minor quirk (I'm one of those pesky developers who believes that as long as the darn application works right on the major things, like its intended purpose, trivial things like the user getting a pretty "It's working, dummy" can break.)

However, now I'm sitting here, having been watching the progress of the file through Konqueror, and I'm getting concerned.  As I type this, the "new.virtual.disk" is up to 5.6 GB and I can hear the ol' hard drive writing, writing away.  

I'm posting a screenshot with this..am I just being nuts or is this a problem? Something I'm doing wrong, perhaps? I'm thinking it should have stopped around 1.6 GB ago...

I'm going to force it to stop at 7 GB if it hasn't...I don't want it overwriting any data I have on the machine and I only had 7.4 GB free when I started this...

Wow, that's strange... anyhow for now, try using these commands:

```
sudo -s
cd /media/host/wubi/disks
dd if=/dev/zero of=new.virtual.disk bs=1M count=4000
mkfs.ext3 -F new.virtual.disk
mkdir /media/extra
mount -o loop,sync /media/host/wubi/disks/new.virtual.disk /media/extra
rsync -avx --exclude '/sys/*' --exclude '/proc/*' / /media/extra
```

is the size 4GB when you do it like that?

also, perhaps doing it with a sparse file-allocation will be faster and work better, just do the same thing as above, only replace the line

```
dd if=/dev/zero of=new.virtual.disk bs=1M count=4000
```

with

```
dd if=/dev/zero of=new.virtual.disk bs=1 seek=4G count=0
```

then reboot back into Windows and backup home.virtual.disk and rename C:\wubi\new.virtual.disk to home.virtual.disk

---

### Post by tuxcantfly on 2007-09-09
> **theartak said:**
> These particular instructions you gave me...the ones I quote in this post....they were for system.virtual.disk, weren't they?

Yes, the instructions for home.virtual.disk are:

```
rsync -avx /home/ /media/extra
```

### Post by tuxcantfly on 2007-09-09
> If everything really is OK but I find I want more space allocated to Windows, how do I do that? ntfsprog?

Boot the partition manager, open GParted, shrink one of your existing drives (using the resize option), that'll leave some unallocated disk space, which you can expand your Windows partition into to use.

---

### Post by tuxcantfly on 2007-09-09
> **hhh said:**
> Dammit dammit dammit dammit. I'm an impatient idiot. Not even an hour later and I've trashed my system. Here's how it happened...

1) Reread this thread top to bottom, came across this post...
[http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=3242011&postcount=78](http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=3242011&postcount=78)
..and wondered if I had installed an outdated version of the partition manager.
2) Read this post...
[http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=3252421&postcount=83](http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=3252421&postcount=83)
...and followed those instructions.
3) Disaster, "Other OS" entries were gone, entering any of the Ubuntu kernels resulted in a GRUB Error 15 (I think it was "File not Found") could only load Partition manager but rebooting afterwards resulted in the same error. Could not enter Windows recovery at startup by pressing F10 anymore.
4) Panicked, and I know this was my ridiculously foolish and crucial error... I entered the partition manager and deleted all partitions except ntfs (sda1) and fat32 (sda2).
5) Complete devestation.  Now booting only shows...

GRUB Loading stage 1.5

GRUB loading, please wait...

Error 22



I now have web access only through a Puppy Live CD I had. I'm pretty sure I have an Ubuntu Live CD at work. Any chance I will be able to restore Windows at least, so I can reinstall Wubi and take it from there?

Lesson - if it ain't broke, don't fix it.

I'm not sure about the first error, GRUB Error 15, but the second error, Error 22, is because you deleted the Ubuntu partiton, on which the GRUB configuration files exist, so GRUB can't start up. Since you're already deleted your Ubuntu partition, you can't restore your Ubuntu install anymore (had you just booted the Super Grub Disk and told it to repair GRUB, that would have fixed it, but too late for that; I've added it to the first post though so others don't make that mistake again).

If you want to restore windows, if you have a Windows XP recovery CD, just boot it, press R to get into recovery mode, then once you get to the prompt, type in:

```
fixmbr
```

and you should be able to boot Windows afterwards

### Post by tuxcantfly on 2007-09-10
> I used version 78 instead of 79 (just a note...there is a huge discrepancy in size between 78 and 79, is all of 79 there? That might explain my earlier issue if it isn't...

Everything is there, I just removed some unused GRLDR files

> What is the proper procedure for purging/reinstalling Partition Manager so other's don't go through what I did?

Synaptic/apt-get/dpkg install/remove are all that should be needed, the instructions you followed were right, and worked fine for others... I still don't know what went wrong in your case, I've never encountered GRUB error 15, I'll see if I can reproduce that error.

> What about the fat32 partition, should I delete that before retrying to make Wubi a permanent Ubuntu install? Any chance that's why I can't grow the ntfs partition?


The NTFS error might be because it needs to be checked and defragmented; just boot Windows, run "chkdsk /f", reboot, let it check the drive, reboot back into Windows again (a 2nd time), run the drive defragmenter, then reboot back to the partition manager, see if that gets it fixed.

> I still can't access my recovery drive (F10 on startup), even though the Windows boot manager is restored. Is that feature gone from my system forever?

That's probably because it needed some custom MBR to boot that. Usually, the recovery software that comes with your new computer has some tools to restore that custom MBR, the computer manual usually says where it is, at least that's how it is on all the Dells, Toshibas, and HPs I've seen.

> When I asked if Partition Manager when installed now automatically partitioned a drive, was that correct or not? If not, how did my drive get repartitioned originally, as I didn't do it?

It isn't supposed to do anything automatically; it's only supposed to do the partitioning after you reboot, specify the partitioning, and press apply. Something went wrong there, I'm not sure if it's just something with your hardware setup or some bug I didn't notice, I'll see if I can find anything.

### Post by tuxcantfly on 2007-09-12
> **lingwu said:**
> Hello,

I'm a linux newbie and has been trying out ubuntu via wubi for a couple weeks now. I've got everything set up to my liking and have learn a lot during this process as well. So having come across lvpm, i thought of moving it to a proper partition. The instructions seem simple enough, so I thought there wouldn't be any problem...but alas...

What i did was I ran the partitioning work on Windows (I used Acronis Partition Manager), set it to 35gb, and set it to format as Ext3. Xp rebooted and did the work no problem.

After that I booted to Ubuntu, looked for Lvpm on Synaptics, found that it was an old version, so I went to sourceforge and download the latest version (79). Ran that, select the correct steps and partition (I made double sure by running fdisk-l) and set it on it's way. Left it running for a couple hours, after I came back, I was pleased to see the promt asking for reboot and didn't show any error messages.

After rebooting I check around, and find that I booted back to the Ubuntu on the virtual disk and not the partitioned Ubuntu! Checking wubi/boot/grub/menu.lst, I find that all the boot options remains pointed at the virtual disks. (at wubi/boot)

Did I mess up somewhere?

Does the GRUB menu show up when you boot your computer? It should have Ubuntu listed on top. The reason why the wubi/boot/grub/menu.lst in Windows still points at the virtual disks are because that's the old Wubi installation; LVPM doesn't delete the original Wubi install.

To check to make sure whether or not you're booting into the real-partition install or the loopmounted one, use this command:

```
cat /proc/mounts

```
And check the output, if it contains /media/host/wubi/disks/system.virtual.disk then it's the loopmounted install, otherwise, if it doesn't have that line and it has something like /dev/disk-by-uuid... / .... it's the real-partition install (in which case you don't have a problem, and you can just uninstall the original Wubi install from Windows to end up with only the real install).

Anyhow the issue could either be that the install didn't get copied over, or that GRUB didn't get installed. To see if the install got copied over, boot Ubuntu, and you should be able to see an additional partition under places -> computer, mount it and see if it has the necessary files in it; namely, if it has a boot folder, and if it has grub/menu.lst within that boot folder (in the partition's folder, like /media/disk/boot/grub/menu.lst, not in /boot), see if that looks correct (check the end, the second line in each entry, after title, should be "root (hd0,0)" or so, not "find --set-root --ignore-floppies /wubi/boot/linux").

If it does, then the issue is simply that GRUB didn't get installed to the MBR for some reason, to get grub installed to the MBR, try this:

```
sudo grub-install /dev/sda --root-directory=/media/disk
```

Then reboot and see if the GRUB menu shows up. In that command, I'm assuming your hard drive is /dev/sda, and that it's mounted at /media/disk, adjust the parameters accordingly, if you don't know if the hard drive is /dev/sda or something else, use the command:
```

sudo fdisk -l | grep "Disk /dev/"
```

And that'll tell you what it is. Also, if that doesn't work either, see if the Super Grub Disk is able to boot it, it can recover and repair GRUB installs.

---

### Post by wmikes on 2007-09-17
ok, i have one hard drive and it is partitioned as c, d, x.  c has windows on it, d has windows apps/data and x is freshly formatted.  x is a 20gb partition with a 1gb swap inside.  when i run wubi and follow the instructions to run lvpm it says to select a target partition.  
i have 5 choices:

/dev/hda1
/dev/hda2
/dev/hda3
/dev/hda4
/dev/hda5

so which one is x?  
am i right in thinking:  /dev/hda3?
none of the volumes have labels even though they are labeled in windows.

i would hate to guess wrong and wipe wubi and windows at the same time.
thanks in advance, MIKE...

---

### Post by tuxcantfly on 2007-09-17
> **wmikes said:**
> ok, i have one hard drive and it is partitioned as c, d, x.  c has windows on it, d has windows apps/data and x is freshly formatted.  x is a 20gb partition with a 1gb swap inside.  when i run wubi and follow the instructions to run lvpm it says to select a target partition.  
i have 5 choices:

/dev/hda1
/dev/hda2
/dev/hda3
/dev/hda4
/dev/hda5

so which one is x?  
am i right in thinking:  /dev/hda3?
none of the volumes have labels even though they are labeled in windows.

i would hate to guess wrong and wipe wubi and windows at the same time.
thanks in advance, MIKE...

/dev/hda1 refers to the first partition, hda2 is the second, etc. Just mount each of the partitions and check their contents, that way you'll be able to see which one it is based on the files in it. Also, if you happen to know the size of the partitions, you can use the command "**df**" and you'll be able to figure out the partition number based on the size of each partition (size, in KB, is listed on second column).

---

### Post by tuxcantfly on 2007-10-13
> **Tamise said:**
>  set my new partition as the boot partition

Yes, that seems to be the problem; since Ubuntu installs GRUB (the bootloader) to the MBR, the partition doesn't have to be set as bootable; in fact, if you do set it as bootable, it'll prevent Windows from booting.

---

### Post by Romanus81 on 2007-10-15
This doesn't have anything to do with LVPM, but that partition manager tool is probably one of the most useful things I have downloaded on Linux next to Wubi, since it allowed me to manage my partitions without the need to make a livecd/usb. Is there any way we could get it with Parted Magic 1.8? They added Partition Image which I use as my backup manager. 
I downloaded the PXE version from the Parted Magic website, it came with 3 files, bzImage, initrd.gz, and sample_pxelinux.cfg, which looked a lot like the menu_pm.lst included with the Partition manager tool.

```
default pmagic
label pmagic
  kernel /pmagic/bzImage
  append noapic initrd=/pmagic/initrd.gz root=/dev/ram0 init=/linuxrc ramdisk_size=100000
```

I tried modifying my grub and everything to see if I could make it work, but I don't know much about PXE or grub. Is there anything you could do to help me?


Here's a link to the PXE version download: [http://www.download.com/Parted-Magic-PXE/3000-2094-10700874.html?part=dl-PartedMag&subj=dl&tag=button](http://www.download.com/Parted-Magic-PXE/3000-2094-10700874.html?part=dl-PartedMag&subj=dl&tag=button)

### Post by jshbbe on 2007-10-19

### Post by tuxcantfly on 2007-10-19
> **jshbbe said:**
> I've been thinking about using LVPM to change my Wubi installation to a real installation, so I downloaded the Partition Manager.  However, when I reboot and select the Partition Manager it gives me the error that it wasn't able to load Windows.

I have Windows Vista, so maybe it is something to do with that. I have over 60 GB free so I would think I had enough space.  Any help would be appreciated.

1. Did you install the deb package from within Ubuntu or the exe installer from Windows when installing UNetbootin? The exe version isn't going to work without a few hacks on Windows Vista (haven't added support for Vista yet), so use the deb version if you didn't do so already.

2. What exactly was the "error that it wasn't able to load Windows." and at what phase did it occur? Was it during the Windows bootloader stage, the GRUB bootloader stage, while partedmagic was booting, within GParted, or while resizing the partition?

Anyhow perhaps try doing a chkdsk /f and defragment your hard drive and try using Vista's disk management utility to shrink the partition size again; that'll probably work better than the partition manager tool.

### Post by tuxcantfly on 2007-10-20
> **jshbbe said:**
> I used the exe for windows.  I did try the deb at first, but when I rebooted I didn't see any option for the Partition Manager.

That's probably the issue. Try using the .deb file, and when you reboot, select Ubuntu first, then Partition Manager will be in the submenu.

Anyhow, worst-case scenario is that you could just try burning the Ubuntu Desktop CD, and it also has GParted on it so it'll let you resize your partitions (though given the erratic behavior of the Vista partition manager, GParted might not help all that much if it is indeed some issue with your partitions, but doesn't hurt to try).

> By the way, if I would install Ubuntu first would I be able to install Windows later if I need to?

Yes, see [https://help.ubuntu.com/community/RecoveringUbuntuAfterInstallingWindows](https://help.ubuntu.com/community/RecoveringUbuntuAfterInstallingWindows)

### Post by tuxcantfly on 2007-11-05
> **kloudy said:**
> I am happy to have Ubuntu Gutsy running as a stand-alone application.  It definitely boots up faster and without a lot of garbage being displayed on the screen the way the WUBI install did..

I am still learning and have a question about PC booting.  I edited the GRUB file on booting to get Windows to be the first choice as default and to give me 10 seconds to decide differently.  I wanted this because I still rely on MSW for MS Money and a few photo editing programs.  After some time, I know I will get used to Linux replacement programs.

Since I use GRUB, I guess this means that if my Ubuntu partition would ever get hosed, I could not start Windows either.  Is that correct?  Under WUBI, Windows was always in control of the boot process.

If I ever delete Ubuntu, how do I get Windows back in charge of the boot process?

Boot up a windows xp/vista recovery cd, go into recovery mode, and enter the command "fixmbr", that'll remove grub and restore the windows bootloader to the mbr, making your system boot straight to windows (though you won't be able to boot ubuntu anymore). Alternatively, should you happen to have just messed up your grub bootloader config, and want to repair it so that you don't have to remove and re-install ubuntu, you can boot using the super grub disk at [http://supergrub.forjamari.linex.org/](http://supergrub.forjamari.linex.org/) and use the "repair" option, or just use it as a temporary bootloader for ubuntu/windows until you fix the bootloader config

> **orengolan said:**
> thanks for a great tutorial.  I installed ubuntu on my fujitsu Q2010!

partition magic (sda4-12GB and sda3-1GB) and then run LVPM. 
later on I uninstall wubi from the windows OS.

1. I have 2 folders on my ubuntu desktop - host0 and disk.
(look at the picture)
what are they and can I delete them or at least not show them on the desktop?
2. when running gparted, it looks like the 1GB partition is not mounted.
does it mean that it's not used?
I wanted it to be the swap partition.  how do I do it?
3. I took a picture of the system monitor.  it shows 3 devices.  

to sum it up, I am not sure what's going on
here and I would like to get some advice.

[IMG]http://ubuntuforums.org/g/images/249002/large/1_desktop.png[/IMG]

1. Edit /etc/fstab, and remove the lines containing /media/host0 and /media/disk
2. Format that 1 GB partition as swap (it's currently formatted as ext3), then add it to the /etc/fstab
3. Will be eliminated after you follow step 2

### Post by orengolan on 2007-11-12

### Post by tuxcantfly on 2007-11-12
> **orengolan said:**
> here is my fstab file:

```
# <file system> <mount point>   <type>  <options>       <dump>  <pass>
proc            /proc           proc        defaults    0   0
# /dev/sda4
UUID=ac7be73e-486e-4b18-937c-d0b840e26a9a     /               ext3        defaults,errors=remount-ro    0   1
# /dev/sda1
UUID=0AC457FFC457EB87       /media/host0       ntfs-3g         defaults      0   0

```

1. should I comment the last line?
2. what about media/disk? I can't see this text in the file.
can u tell me what am I doing?

thanks!

Just open GParted, format your /dev/sda3 from ext3 to swap, then change your /etc/fstab to look like this:

```
# <file system> <mount point>   <type>  <options>       <dump>  <pass>
proc            /proc           proc        defaults    0   0
# /dev/sda4
UUID=ac7be73e-486e-4b18-937c-d0b840e26a9a     /               ext3        defaults,errors=remount-ro    0   1
# /dev/sda3
UUID=someuuid   none swap sw 0 0
```

substitute "someuuid" for whatever the output of sudo vol_id -u /dev/sda3 is, after it's been formatted as swap

---

### Post by tuxcantfly on 2007-11-13
> **orengolan said:**
> I followed your steps and when I open the system monitor it shows the root device only.  interestingly, after running gparted, another device is added - sd2 in /media/disk.

That's apparently the Windows drive, which was previously mounted at /media/host0. When you run GParted and it scans for new disks, it'll automatcially mount it. Solution is just to right-click, unmount, or not to run GParted in the first place.

> what is this disk folder? can I get rid of this icon? (it's on my desktop)

If you want to get rid of ALL hard drive and other volume icons from ever appearing on your desktop (though note that that'll mean CD, USB drive, and other icons for removable media won't show up), run "gconf-editor", go to apps -> nautilus -> desktop, and uncheck "volumes visible". The folder location itself is in /media though the folder is auto-generated; therefore it's pointless to try deleting it.

> the gparted shows the swap partition and tell me that it's active.
does it mean I am ok?

yes that means the swap is working and activated

---

### Post by stiboy on 2007-12-05
Okay I've searched and searched for a solution to my problem, but to no avail. Here it is in a nutshell. Wubi was a perfect solution for me to install Ubuntu on my computer with no cd drive, however I wanted to move the install to a dedicated partition and perhaps do away with evil :twisted:Windows:twisted: altogether. I followed the instruction in the thread and i even watched the video. However, the process stops at the same point every time. I boot into the partition manager program. ### Post by tuxcantfly on 2007-12-05
> **stiboy said:**
> Okay I've searched and searched for a solution to my problem, but to no avail. Here it is in a nutshell. Wubi was a perfect solution for me to install Ubuntu on my computer with no cd drive, however I wanted to move the install to a dedicated partition and perhaps do away with evil :twisted:Windows:twisted: altogether. I followed the instruction in the thread and i even watched the video. However, the process stops at the same point every time. I boot into the partition manager program. It comes up with a screen asking me to select a resolution I do so then it asks for a screen depth and I choose one. At this point the program should kick in to gear and I should be able to access resizing features and so forth, however after choosing a screen depth the screen goes blank and that's the end of story. The only out of the blank screen is ctrl+alt+del which reboots. My first thought was to try a different depth. I tried them all and none worked. I even tried a lower resolution and that didn't work either. Has anyone else experienced this problem, and if so, were you able to get it to work and how?  Thanks.

Apparently, the xvesa server doesn't seem to like your graphics card (which is strange, since that's supposed to be almost universally compatible). Seems like you may want to try the xorg xserver instead of the xvesa one, since it appears to be working on Ubuntu.

When in the boot menu, right after selecting the "partition manager" boot entry, hammer away at the "esc" button. That should present you with a menu that allows you to edit the boot options. There should be one option that begins with "kernel" and has a long list of options afterwards. Highlight that line, and press "e" to begin editing it, remove the option "xvesa" from the list (it should be towards the end), and press "enter" to save the changes, then press "b" to boot, that should allow you to boot properly.

If it still doesn't work, then just burn an Ubuntu CD and use the partition manager there, or if using Vista, you can use its partition manager instead. If you can't use a CD, perhaps try running Ubuntu or any other Linux distro with GParted off a USB drive.

---

### Post by tuxcantfly on 2007-12-16
> **gotee12 said:**
> I've notice on another post that you (tuxcantfly) replied that LVPM doesn't support Wubi 7.10 yet. I'm getting the infamous "You are running LVPM on a host installation. You must run it on a loopmounted install" message when I try to move my Wubi-fied 7.10 install over to my newly created partitions.

Any idea as to when LVPM will be compatible with a Wubi-installed Ubuntu 7.10? Oh, and I'm not trying to nag, I realize there's more to life than this, especially during Christmas! Thanx!

I'll get around to it in January or so; I have little spare time these days with holiday and college-application-deadline seasons coming up; I don't want to rush out buggy, untested software that could potentially break thousands of computers. Until then, to migrate Wubi installs (any version, works on both 7.04 or 7.10), data, and settings (apps can be quickly reinstalled via apt-get) to dedicated-partition installs without needing a CD:

1. Create 3 new partitions with the [Partition Manager](http://lubi.sourceforge.net/lvpm.html) ([download](http://sourceforge.net/project/showfiles.php?group_id=198821&package_id=240127)): a 5-10 GB (ext3 format) partition to use as root (/), a ~1 GB (equal to RAM size) (swap format) partition to use as swap, and make the rest a (ext3 format) partition to use as /home.

2. Boot back into the Wubi-generated Ubuntu install, mount the new partition that will be used as /home in the dedicated-partition install to /media/disk, and copy the contents of the current /home recursively over to the new partition:

```
rsync -avx /home/ /media/disk
```

3. Reboot into Windows, and install [UNetbootin](http://lubi.sourceforge.net/unetbootin.html) ([download Ubuntu 7.10 version](http://sourceforge.net/project/showfiles.php?group_id=198821&package_id=243411)),  ([download versions for Ubuntu 7.04 and other distros like openSUSE and Fedora](http://sourceforge.net/project/showfiles.php?group_id=198821)).

Download and install the .exe version, reboot, then select "UNetbootin" at the boot menu, then the Ubuntu installer will start up. After that, just follow the standard Ubuntu installation process ([guide](http://www.howtoforge.com/unetbootin_windows_ubuntu_fedora)), just make sure that at the "partitioning" stage, select the "manual" option, and make sure tospecify the appropriate mountpoints (make sure the partition you copies /home to is mounted at /home, and make sure it doesn't get formatted). After that, wait for Ubuntu to be downloaded and installed from the net (it'll take a long time if you're on a slow connection, just give it a few hours to complete).

4. Once done installing, reboot back, and your new dedicated-partition Ubuntu install, complete with data and settings preserved, should be there. You can re-install the individual applications via apt-get. Once done, you can reboot back into Windows and remove the UNetbootin installer (it'll prompt on startup), and remove Wubi, then you'll be done.

---

### Post by tuxcantfly on 2008-01-03
> **1John said:**
> This is my first post on forums, please be patient as I am new to ubuntu.
I tried to upgrade wubi 7.04  to real partitions. I know I made some mistakes following your clear instructions but below is what I actually did. 
First I shrank my windows xp partition (hda1) from 200gb to 160gb using parted magic. Then I created an extended partition (hda2) on the available 40gb which i split into 3 logical partitions:-
hda 5 = 10gb ext3 intended for ubuntu root
hda 6 = 2gb linux swap
hda 7 = approx 28gb ext3 intended for /user

As a small side note, it's /home not /user (/usr maybe?) you should be isolating.

> I then rebooted to my 7.04 wubi. I had already obtained most recent version of LVPM which I used to transfer to hda 5. I realised I would not be able to use the intended /user drive and assumed everthing would go on hda5 instead
Everything appeared to work OK right through to installing grub. However when I boot into ubuntu using grub I think I get the original wubi installation plus the use of the swap partition.  I think this is because of the size of the partition.

How can rescue this situation. Please remember that I am new to linux.
With hindsight I can see the mistake I made in not creating a new primary partition but now I am not sure what to do.
_________
Have rebooted using parted magic and mounted hda5 which is shown as Debian and contains 167752items 6.4gb free space 4.8gb this seems to include normal directory structure e.g.\home has 5243items 301.3mb.
While there I checked hda7 which is empty EXT3 with only lost+found directory.
____________
I am now convinced that the lvpm wubi move did actually work as it should (despite my mistakes) and I was just a little confused.

Seems like the GRUB bootloader didn't get installed properly. Try this to see if the install was indeed properly transferred over:

When you get to the GRUB menu (if you don't see a grub menu, select the wubi option in the Windows boot menu, then hammer away at ESC, it should get you there), press c for a command line. Then enter these commands:

```
root (hd0,4)
configfile /boot/grub/menu.lst
```

This basically asks grub to continue on with the configuration from the actual partition. If it works, and you're then in the dedicated-partition install (you can check this by opening system-> administration -> system monitor, go to filesystems, it should say /dev/hda5 not /media/host/wubi/disks/system.virtual.disk or anything like that) then that's good, all you have to do is open up a commandline then enter ```
sudo grub-install /dev/hda
``` and you should be good to go

If, however, it didn't work at the grub commandline stage, that means something went wrong. Given the sheer number of things that could have gone wrong, I'd just try again using the alternative instructions in my first post (the temporary ones intended for Wubi 7.10, using UNetbootin to install to a partition cleanly and then copying back the /home diretory), they should work more reliably than LVPM.

> Is there an easy way to now move the /home directory currently on hda5 to the empty spare logical partition on hda 7.

I'd just delete the partition intended for /home (hda7) and expand / (hda5) to fill up the freed space. Since the upcoming Ubuntu 8.04 is slated to have support for preserving the /home subdirectory in the / filesystem during installation (details at [https://wiki.ubuntu.com/UbiquityPreserveHome](https://wiki.ubuntu.com/UbiquityPreserveHome) ), I really don't see the need for a dedicated /home.

However, if you do indeed want a dedicated /home, simply mount /dev/hda7 somewhere (in this example I'll use /media/extra), and then use the command ```
sudo rsync -avx /home/ /media/extra
``` and that will sync over the contents of /home to the partition, then you can delete the contents of /home (but keep the empty /home directory itself), and then edit /etc/fstab and add an entry to mount the new partition at the end. It should look something like (check the last line, that's the one you want to add):

```
# /etc/fstab: static file system information.
#
# <file system> <mount point>   <type>  <options>       <dump>  <pass>
proc            /proc           proc    defaults        0       0
/dev/hda5    /            ext3         defaults         0        0
/dev/hda7    /home    ext3        defaults         0        0
```

Then reboot and it should work. Note that if your fstab is using UUIDs, you'll have to change the last entry to look like (replace the part after UUID= with the /home partition's UUID, you can determine that using```
 sudo vol_id -u /dev/hda7
```

```
# /dev/hda7
UUID=2d636703-d71b-4f80-ac94-18e1dc9032d4    /home    ext3        defaults         0        0
```

> Sorry for any confusion but thanks for producing software that allows a windows user to suck and see what Ubuntu is really like and then keep eveything in a complete install. I am looking forward to the day I will be able to delete the windows partition completely.

Just out of interest - I had to redo links back to the windows partition (I had 'my documents' and 'shared documents' links on the desktop) and I lost all the library entries in Rhythmbox presumably because I had just scanned 'my music' folder rather than importing the music. I expect I will be able to work out how to scan the folder again to rebuild the library.

That's because the mountpoint for the Windows partition changed (from /media/host to /media/host0), so the links are probably broken now. You can either re-create the links, or symlink /media/host0 to /media/host ```
sudo ln -s /media/host0 /media/host
``` though that might cause issues later on (since the existence of /media/host/wubi is often used to check if the install is a loopmounted one, so your dedicated-partition install might get mistaken for a loopmounted one).

### Post by tuxcantfly on 2008-01-04

Is there a way to quickly backup my Wubi install to an external drive? I've tried (in Windows) copying the C:\Ubuntu folder and associated boot files (wu*, boot.ini) but it fails when trying to copy the home.disk. It gives a free space error every time, even though there is roughly 160GB free on the external drive.

I was hoping I could simply copy the C:\Ubuntu folder and associated boot files to an external drive as a quick and dirty backup. My main impetus for this was to offer my Wubi install as a guinea pig for your 7.10 version of LVPM, seeing as how I could simply "restore" the Ubuntu folder and files off of the external drive if the LVPM transfer failed.

I'm wondering if it's a Windows permissions problem but I don't want to arbitrarily add an NTFS account with full access to the Ubuntu folder not knowing what the outcome would be. Thanx!

That external drive wouldn't happen to be formatted as FAT32, would it? FAT32 has a file size limit of 4 GB or so, so that's probably why it can't copy over the home.disk (exceeds maximum supported file size). Perhaps just shrink part of the FAT32 partition and format it as NTFS, UDF, or EXT3; those can store larger filesizes.

**Attention all Alpha Software Testers aka Guinea Pigs!**

See here: [https://sourceforge.net/project/showfiles.php?group_id=198821&package_id=238165](https://sourceforge.net/project/showfiles.php?group_id=198821&package_id=238165) for the highly, extremely experimental Wubi-7.10 compatible LVPM version (the one with the nice ALPHA in the filename)

Make sure you have the usual slew of recovery tools with you (Ubuntu 7.10 Desktop CD, Windows recovery disk for fixing a botched MBR, and a Super Grub Disk), just in case.

To get more detailed information while running, run it from the commandline using ```
sudo lvpm
```

Not for the faint of heart; use the more reliable alternative instructions in the first post if having the slightest doubt.

EDIT: There were a couple of bugs in the older version I uploaded (pre-90) (resulting from a few issues here in keeping bzr local and remote branches synced); it'll take a few grub hacks to get it to boot on certain disk configurations, and the /home partition's contents weren't synced over properly. These bugs shouldn't be present in the latest version on sourceforge. If you used the older version and are having issues, correct the problems manually or try again with the latest one.

### Post by tuxcantfly on 2008-01-26
> **HHelsinger said:**
> I was using LVPM to resize my Wubi install, so that _Remastersys_ would run properly -- _Remastersys_ had  hung in the middle of the install, and when I posted a query on the Remastersys forum the conjecture was that it needed more space.

So I enlarged my Wubi home.disk from 1.9 Gig to 2.9 Gig.  That worked fine, but it didn't help _remastersys_ any.

So then I enlarged root.disk from 11.2 gig to 18gig.  That seemed to work, but when, after changing the file names in Windows I try to reboot into Wubi/Ubuntu I get a fatal error message that .
The error message suggests using e2fsck, but that doesn't help any.

Basically, when LVPM resizes my root.disk the result won't boot, because it can't find the superblock.   I've tried this several times with the same result.   Any ideas what is going on, and how to avoid it?

Thanks.

Perhaps it might work if you try doing the process manually, or at least you'll be able to see what's going wrong. In a nutshell:

1. Create a new root.disk:
[https://wiki.ubuntu.com/WubiGuide#head-5aac3daad4eb9fcc3502ba1a4d6891b71b050b1d](https://wiki.ubuntu.com/WubiGuide#head-5aac3daad4eb9fcc3502ba1a4d6891b71b050b1d)

2. Mount it somewhere:

```
sudo mount -o loop /path/to/root.disk /media/somemountpoint
```

3. Copy over files using rsync:

```
rsync -avx --exclude '/sys/*' --exclude '/proc/*' / /media/somemountpoint
```

See if anything goes wrong, or if you get any error messages that provide any important details.

Also, I doubt that remastersys is going to work properly from a Wubi-generated install, due to the various differences in the boot and mounting process between the standard Ubuntu install and the Wubi one due to the fact that it's running from a disk image not an actual filesystem. You'll probably need to go switch over to a dedicated-partition install (either transfer your existing install over using LVPM or do a new install using UNetbootin, both are in my sig) in order to be able to properly remaster your install.

### Post by tuxcantfly on 2008-01-29
> **HHelsinger said:**
> This is still proving a problem.   So I decided to do an install and transfer to a dedicated partition.  I cleaned up the disk, made lots of space on the disk, and then tried to download gparted or whatever partition manager I was supposed to use.   And the message I got said there isn't enough disk space!   Indeed, the system manager shows my Wubi/Ubuntu root as 100% full. See the attached image.

Could this be part of why I can't resize it?  Can you suggest how I can free up some space in the root.disk?
Files to delete?  whatever?

thanks.

You're still booting off the Wubi-generated loopmounted-install system (as shown by the /host/ubuntu/disks/root.disk under device, not /dev/sda3 or the like). If I understand well, you haven't yet transferred the install over to a dedicated partition, and you are unable to install a partition manager (gparted) within the Wubi/Ubuntu root. If so, remove a few packages that you aren't using at the moment within Ubuntu (openoffice comes to mind, removing it will save you a few hundred MB; you can re-install it after transferring), so that you'll have enough space to install the LVPM package and for the temporary files created during the transfer process.

Then, reboot into Windows, and install the .exe version of this package (this includes GParted, normally the .deb version would be used but you're running low on space so the Windows version can be used): [http://sourceforge.net/project/showfiles.php?group_id=198821&package_id=240127](http://sourceforge.net/project/showfiles.php?group_id=198821&package_id=240127)

Then reboot again, boot into the UNetbootin menu option, that'll let you start GParted and resize your partitions and create new ones as described at [http://lubi.sourceforge.net/lvpm.html](http://lubi.sourceforge.net/lvpm.html)

Then reboot back into Ubuntu, install the LVPM package (remember you'll want the one labeled 7.10-ALPHA since you're running Wubi 7.10), and after that all should be the same as instructions on the site.

Otherwise, if all else fails, reboot back into Windows, and install the UNetbootin Ubuntu 7.10 package at [http://lubi.sourceforge.net/unetbootin.html](http://lubi.sourceforge.net/unetbootin.html) that'll let you install Ubuntu directly to a dedicated-partition install; this will let you start with a clean, standard install (just re-install the packages you need).

### Post by tuxcantfly on 2008-01-31
> **HHelsinger said:**
